ca"><div class="ch bg fy fz ga gb"><h1 id="2e76" class="oq or gt be os ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn bj">Table of Contents</h1><ol class=""><li id="8bd4" class="mk ml bl on oo"></span></div><div class="gm gn go gp gq"><div class="ab ca"><div class="ch bg fy fz ga gb"><h1 id="41ab" class="oq or gt be os ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn bj">Introduction</h1><p id="19bf" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn po mp mq mr pp mt mu mv pq mx my mz pr nb nc nd ps nf ng nh gm bj">Elastic Beanstalk is a cloud service that allows deployment and management the web applications without the user worrying about the underlying infrastructure.</p><p id="fcb3" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">Elastic Beanstalk provides the following benefits for a Streamlit application:</p><ul class=""><li id="881d" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj"><strong class="mm gu">Scalability</strong>: Elastic Beanstalk automatically scales the application up or down based on traffic and demand.</li><li id="5906" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj"><strong class="mm gu">Reliability</strong>: Elastic Beanstalk monitors the application and ensures its availability and performance.</li><li id="8e0e" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj"><strong class="mm gu">Security</strong>: Elastic Beanstalk secures the application with firewalls, encryption, and access control.</li><li id="c6bd" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj"><strong class="mm gu">Flexibility</strong>: Elastic Beanstalk supports the application via various platforms and languages, such as Python, and Docker.</li></ul><p id="7797" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">The following diagram illustrates the workflow of Elastic Beanstalk.</p><figure class="nl nm nn no np nq ni nj paragraph-image"><div class="ni nj pu"><picture><source srcSet="https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:640/format:webp/1*3N0PuVc6AqfpdfXuZSKF5w.png 640w, workflow</figcaption></figure></div></div></div><div class="ab ca oi oj ok ol" role="separator"><span class="om bx bl on oo op"></span><span class="om bx bl on oo op"></span><span class="om bx bl on oo"></span></div><div class="gm gn go gp gq"><div class="ab ca"><div class="ch bg fy fz ga gb"><h1 id="22fb" class="oq or gt be os ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn bj">Prerequisites</h1><p id="0f00" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn po mp mq mr pp mt mu mv pq mx my mz pr nb nc nd ps nf ng nh gm bj">This section lists the requirements for deploying the application, such as:</p><ol class=""><li id="6ebe" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh pt ob oc bj">Active <a class="af pv" href="https://aws.amazon.com/" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank"><strong class="mm gu">AWS Account</strong></a>.</li><li id="dda9" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh pt ob oc bj">Roles and Permissions</li><li id="9396" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh pt ob oc bj">Custom <a class="af pv" href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/vpc/latest/userguide/create-vpc.html#create-vpc-and-other-resources" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank"><strong class="mm gu">Virtual Private Network (VPC)</strong></a>. Ensure that under <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">NAT Gateways</em></strong>, you choose <code class="cw px py pz qa b">In 1 AZ</code>.</li><li id="8edf" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh pt ob oc bj">Create an <strong class="mm gu">application source bundle that</strong> follows the <a class="af pv" href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/elasticbeanstalk/latest/dg/applications-sourcebundle.html" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">criteria and requirements defined here</a> when deploying the application or its version with the AWS Elastic Beanstalk console.</li><li id="fe00" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh pt ob oc bj"><strong class="mm gu">EB CLI (<em class="pw">Optional</em>)</strong>: Install the EB CLI, which extends the AWS CLI and provides commands specifically for managing the Elastic Beanstalk environments.</li></ol></div></div></div><div class="ab ca oi oj ok ol" role="separator"><span class="om bx bl on oo op"></span><span class="om bx bl on oo op"></span><span class="om bx bl on oo"></span></div><div class="gm gn go gp gq"><div class="ab ca"><div class="ch bg fy fz ga gb"><h1 id="ffb6" class="oq or gt be os ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn bj">Setting Up Roles and Permissions</h1><p id="d6b3" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn po mp mq mr pp mt mu mv pq mx my mz pr nb nc nd ps nf ng nh gm bj">This section describes the necessary roles and permissions that should be provided to you as an IAM user by your Account admin.</p><h2 id="31cf" class="qb or gt be os qc qd dx ow qe qf dz pa mv qg qh qi mz qj qk ql nd qm qn qo qp bj">Admin Setup</h2><p id="db69" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn po mp mq mr pp mt mu mv pq mx my mz pr nb nc nd ps nf ng nh gm bj">Your account Admin should create or add the following policies and attach them to your <strong class="mm gu">IAM User</strong> name</p><ul class=""><li id="205c" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj"><code class="cw px py pz qa b">AdministratorAccess-AWSElasticBeanstalk</code></li><li id="285f" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj"><code class="cw px py pz qa b">AmazonS3FullAccess</code></li><li id="2155" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Create a least privilege <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">IAM policy</em></strong> with the policies found <a class="af pv" href="https://github.com/Ndaruga/streamlit-CICD/blob/main/IAM-user-access-policy.json" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">here</a>:</li></ul><h2 id="af37" class="qb or gt be os qc qd dx ow qe qf dz pa mv qg qh qi mz qj qk ql nd qm qn qo qp bj">IAM User setup</h2><p id="7005" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn po mp mq mr pp mt mu mv pq mx my mz pr nb nc nd ps nf ng nh gm bj">As an IAM user with the permissions granted above, you should create a Customer-managed<em class="pw"> </em><a class="af pv" href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/elasticbeanstalk/latest/dg/iam-instanceprofile.html#iam-instanceprofile-create" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank"><em class="pw">Instance Profile</em></a><em class="pw"> role</em> and name it <code class="cw px py pz qa b"><strong class="mm gu">aws-elasticbeanstalk-ec2-role</strong></code>. Attach the following policies:</p><ul class=""><li id="96e2" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj"><code class="cw px py pz qa b">AWSElasticBeanstalkWebTier</code></li><li id="e784" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj"><code class="cw px py pz qa b">AWSElasticBeanstalkMulticontainerDocker</code></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="ab ca oi oj ok ol" role="separator"><span class="om bx bl on oo op"></span><span class="om bx bl on oo op"></span><span class="om bx bl on oo"></span></div><div class="gm gn go gp gq"><div class="ab ca"><div class="ch bg fy fz ga gb"><h1 id="7bfb" class="oq or gt be os ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn bj">Creating the Elastic Beanstalk environment</h1><p id="32b4" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn po mp mq mr pp mt mu mv pq mx my mz pr nb nc nd ps nf ng nh gm bj">This section describes how to initialize and create an Elastic Beanstalk environment for the application. It also explains how to configure the environment settings, such as the load balancer, security group, port, and CORS.</p><h2 id="efe3" class="qb or gt be os qc qd dx ow qe qf dz pa mv qg qh qi mz qj qk ql nd qm qn qo qp bj">Configuring the environment through the AWS Console</h2><p id="1aae" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn po mp mq mr pp mt mu mv pq mx my mz pr nb nc nd ps nf ng nh gm bj">To start configuring the environment from the console, you need to have either of the following</p><ul class=""><li id="4dbd" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Zip the folder files and store the zip file locally.</li><li id="214b" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Upload the zip file or entire folder containing the application files on a S3 Bucket</li></ul><p id="e550" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">To configure,</p><ol class=""><li id="50f0" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh pt ob oc bj">Log in to your <a class="af pv" href="https://aws.amazon.com/" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">AWS console</a> and select your preferred region from the top right of the navigation menu.</li><li id="337d" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh pt ob oc bj">Once the region is selected, still in the navigation bar, click on the services or Search icons and type <em class="pw">Elastic Beanstalk</em>.</li><li id="cbb7" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh pt ob oc bj">Click on the <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Elastic beanstalk</code> from the list, and click <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Create Application</code></li></ol><p id="b41f" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj"><strong class="mm gu">Step 1: Configure the environment</strong></p><p id="56cf" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">Amazon Elastic Beanstalk has two types of environment tiers to support different types of applications: <a class="af pv" href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/elasticbeanstalk/latest/dg/concepts-webserver.html" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank"><em class="pw">Web server environment</em></a> and <a class="af pv" href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/elasticbeanstalk/latest/dg/concepts-worker.html" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank"><em class="pw">Worker environment</em></a>.</p><ol class=""><li id="98e7" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh pt ob oc bj">Under <strong class="mm gu">Environment Tier</strong>, select <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Web Server Environment</code>. This is because the application will serve an HTTP request to the user before processing any workload.</li><li id="b721" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh pt ob oc bj">Under <strong class="mm gu">Application information</strong>, give the application a descriptive name. Optionally, you could provide any application tags related to the EB environment.</li><li id="c2ff" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh pt ob oc bj">In the <strong class="mm gu">Environment information</strong> section,</li></ol><ul class=""><li id="b64c" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Environment name,</em></strong> you could choose to give your name or leave the already pre-filled name which is your application name with the <em class="pw">“-env”</em> postfix.</li><li id="073c" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Domain</em></strong>, you can choose to leave it blank and in that case, AWS will autogenerate a name for you or provide a domain prefix name. If you provide a custom name, Ensure to check domain availability.</li><li id="6836" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Environment description</em></strong>, optionally provide detailed information on what the application is about.</li></ul><p id="d30f" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">4. In the <strong class="mm gu">Platform</strong> section</p><ul class=""><li id="08d2" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Platform type</em></strong>, select <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Managed platform</code> since we want the platforms to be maintained by AWS</li><li id="0e2c" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Platform</em></strong> in the dropdown list, select <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Docker</code> from the list.</li><li id="b6b9" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Platform Branch</em></strong>, from the drop-down list, select <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Docker running on 64bit Amazon Linux 2023</code></li><li id="cbf0" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Leave the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">platform version</em></strong> with the default selected value.</li></ul><p id="2729" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">5. On the <strong class="mm gu">Application Code</strong> section,</p><ul class=""><li id="ebbc" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Select <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Upload your code</code>.</li><li id="90ef" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">On the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Version label</em></strong> provide a unique version name for your application code.</li><li id="ff63" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">On the Source code origin, select either <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Local file</code> or <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Public S3 URL</code> depending on where you have your code residing.</li></ul><p id="d44a" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">6. In the <strong class="mm gu">Presets</strong> Section, under configuration presets, select <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Custom configuration</code> to avoid using the default EC2 instances configurations.</p><p id="e5ca" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">7. Click <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Next</code> to go to step 2.</p><h2 id="dcf1" class="qb or gt be os qc qd dx ow qe qf dz pa mv qg qh qi mz qj qk ql nd qm qn qo qp bj">Step 2: Configure Service Access</h2><p id="d831" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn po mp mq mr pp mt mu mv pq mx my mz pr nb nc nd ps nf ng nh gm bj">On the <strong class="mm gu">Service access</strong> section,</p><ul class=""><li id="06da" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">service role</em></strong>, if you are creating an elastic beanstalk environment for the first time, select <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Create and use new service role</code>. Otherwise, select <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Use an existing service role</code></li><li id="4453" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Service role name</em></strong>, AWS will autofill the service role name <code class="cw px py pz qa b">aws-elasticbeanstalk-service-role</code>.</li><li id="6c81" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">EC2 Key Pair</em></strong>, you can leave this section blank or select any of the Key pairs you have ever created before.</li><li id="a006" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">EC2 instance profile</em></strong>, select the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">managed policy</em></strong> that you created in the prerequisites. See option</li></ul><h2 id="7c0a" class="qb or gt be os qc qd dx ow qe qf dz pa mv qg qh qi mz qj qk ql nd qm qn qo qp bj">Step 3: Set up the application Networking</h2><p id="66ad" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn po mp mq mr pp mt mu mv pq mx my mz pr nb nc nd ps nf ng nh gm bj">In this Step, we configure the VPC for the environment as well as subnets for the Amazon EC2 instances and the Application load balancer.</p><ol class=""><li id="60bf" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh pt ob oc bj">In the <strong class="mm gu">Virtual Private Cloud (VPC)</strong> section, under the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">VPC</em></strong> option, select the Custom VPC that you had initially created.</li><li id="dfd0" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh pt ob oc bj">In the <strong class="mm gu">Instance Settings</strong> Section,</li></ol><ul class=""><li id="ed7d" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under, <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Public IP Address</em></strong>, check the <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Activated</code> Checkbox to allow you to have access to the EC2 instances during debugging.</li><li id="1dfe" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Instance subnets</em></strong>, check all the availability zones subnets or check only the Public or Private Subnets.</li></ul><p id="0537" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">3. In the <strong class="mm gu">Database settings</strong> section, leave the options as they are since the application does not rely on any database.</p><p id="b1fc" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">4. Click <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Next</code> to go to step 4.</p><h2 id="2203" class="qb or gt be os qc qd dx ow qe qf dz pa mv qg qh qi mz qj qk ql nd qm qn qo qp bj">Step 4: Configure instance traffic and scaling</h2><p id="5e47" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn po mp mq mr pp mt mu mv pq mx my mz pr nb nc nd ps nf ng nh gm bj">Amazon EC2 Auto Scaling helps ensure that you have the correct number of EC2 instances available to handle the load for your application. EC2 instances are organized into Auto Scaling groups, which act as logical units for scaling and management.</p><ol class=""><li id="9265" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh pt ob oc bj">In the <strong class="mm gu">Instances</strong> section,</li></ol><ul class=""><li id="e0ac" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">In <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Root volume (boot device)</em></strong> options:</li><li id="6220" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">From the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Root Volume type</em></strong> dropdown list, select <code class="cw px py pz qa b">General Purpose (SSD)</code></li><li id="bd67" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">For <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Size</em></strong> Assign <code class="cw px py pz qa b">40 GB</code> of the root volume.</li><li id="0c51" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Leave the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Input/output operations per second (IOPS)</em></strong> as blank.</li><li id="1f56" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Leave the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Throughput</em></strong> as the default (125 MiB/s)</li><li id="7bb8" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">In the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Amazon CloudWatch monitoring</em></strong> option, under monitoring interval select <code class="cw px py pz qa b">5 minute</code></li><li id="2c6e" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">On the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Instance metadata service (IMDS)</em></strong>, leave the <code class="cw px py pz qa b">IMDSv1</code> as Deactivated.</li><li id="271e" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">EC2 security groups</em></strong>, ensure you select the security group from the list that allows inbound traffic on <em class="pw">PORT 8501</em></li></ul><p id="52e4" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">2. In the <strong class="mm gu">Capacity</strong> Section, configure the compute capacity for the elastic beanstalk environment as follows:</p><ul class=""><li id="41a4" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">On the <strong class="mm gu">Auto Scaling group</strong></li><li id="caa4" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">under <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Environment type</em></strong>, select <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Load Balanced</code>.</li><li id="ece6" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">In the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">instances</em></strong> option, set the <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Min</code> and <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Max</code> number of instances to be <code class="cw px py pz qa b">1</code> and <code class="cw px py pz qa b">5</code> respectively.</li><li id="de1a" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Fleet Composition</em></strong>, select <code class="cw px py pz qa b">On-Demand instances</code>. This means that all the instances will be running on an on-demand basis.</li><li id="dea3" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Architecture</em></strong>, ensure that <code class="cw px py pz qa b">x86-64</code> is selected to avoid dependency issues from the application&#x27;s code.</li><li id="d1f2" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Instance types</em></strong>, add instances to your fleet. The cost-optimal instance that does not have a significant compromise on performance is <code class="cw px py pz qa b">m5.large</code>. If you choose more than one instance type, AWS will deploy the smallest of your choices.</li><li id="bdb6" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">AMI ID</em></strong>, AWS will choose a Machine Image based on the parameters you have filled before this step.</li><li id="1dc3" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Availability Zones, Placement</em></strong>, leave the default selected values</li><li id="5d63" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Scaling Cooldown</em></strong>, ensure the value is set to <code class="cw px py pz qa b">360 Seconds</code></li><li id="715e" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">On the <strong class="mm gu">Scaling triggers</strong>, ensure that the following default values are left unchanged:</li><li id="9914" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj"><strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Metric</em></strong>: <code class="cw px py pz qa b">NetworkOut</code></li><li id="dfdc" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj"><strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Statistic</em></strong>: <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Average</code></li><li id="5b25" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj"><strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Unit</em></strong>: <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Bytes</code></li><li id="f8e3" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj"><strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Period</em></strong>: <code class="cw px py pz qa b">5 minutes</code></li><li id="985a" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj"><strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Breach duration</em></strong>: <code class="cw px py pz qa b">5 minutes</code></li><li id="7b54" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj"><strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Upper threshold</em></strong>: <code class="cw px py pz qa b">6000000</code></li><li id="7edb" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj"><strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Scale up increment</em></strong>: <code class="cw px py pz qa b">1 EC2 instances</code></li><li id="6919" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj"><strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Lower threshold</em></strong>: <code class="cw px py pz qa b">2000000</code></li><li id="98a3" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj"><strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Scale down increment</em></strong>: <code class="cw px py pz qa b">-1 EC2 instances</code></li></ul><p id="cab7" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">3. In the <strong class="mm gu">Load balancer network settings</strong> section, we configure how and where the load balancer is set within the network.</p><ul class=""><li id="c81f" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Visibility</em></strong>, ensure the load balancer is set to <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Public</code>, for it to serve requests from the internet.</li><li id="1d51" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Load balancer subnets</em></strong>, select <em class="pw">one subnet from each Availability zone</em>.</li></ul><p id="e0fc" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">4. In the <strong class="mm gu">Load Balancer Type</strong> section, ensure you select <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Application load balancer</code>. Also, the Application Loadbalancer should be <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Dedicated</code>.</p><p id="0550" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">5. In the <strong class="mm gu">Listeners</strong> section, You can specify listeners for your load balancer. By default, AWS configures your load balancer with a standard web server on port 80.</p><p id="4026" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">6. In the <strong class="mm gu">Processes, Rules, and Log file access</strong>, leave all the default values, if any.</p><p id="5fc2" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">7. Click <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Next</code> to go to step 5</p><h2 id="db02" class="qb or gt be os qc qd dx ow qe qf dz pa mv qg qh qi mz qj qk ql nd qm qn qo qp bj">Step 5: Configure updates, monitoring, and logging</h2><p id="f8d2" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn po mp mq mr pp mt mu mv pq mx my mz pr nb nc nd ps nf ng nh gm bj">This step is about configuring updates, monitoring, and logging for AWS Elastic Beanstalk environments. It explains the various options and features that users can access to manage their environments and applications.</p><ol class=""><li id="f3a4" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh pt ob oc bj">In the <strong class="mm gu">Monitoring</strong> section,</li></ol><ul class=""><li id="ba2f" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">under <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Health Reporting</em></strong>, select <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Enhanced</code> as the health reporting system.</li><li id="3bd9" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">In the <em class="pw">CloudWatch Custom Metrics — Instance</em> drop-down list, Choose the following metrics:</li><li id="1b22" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">ApplicationRequests2xx</li><li id="f09b" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">ApplicationRequests3xx</li><li id="9466" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">ApplicationRequests4xx</li><li id="f056" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">ApplicationRequests5xx</li><li id="158c" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">CPUIdle</li><li id="16ea" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">InstanceHealth</li><li id="864d" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">In the <em class="pw">CloudWatch Custom Metrics — Environment</em> drop-down list, Choose the following metrics:</li><li id="cbb6" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">ApplicationLatencyP99.9</li><li id="3638" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">InstancesInfo</li><li id="d527" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">InstancesOk</li><li id="2be7" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">InstancesSevere</li><li id="6748" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">InstancesUnknown</li><li id="f96e" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">InstancesWarning</li><li id="7b74" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Leave the values under the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Health monitoring rule customization</em></strong> as Unchecked.</li><li id="b7a0" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">The <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Health event streaming to Cloudwatch Logs</em></strong> options should also remain Unchecked.</li></ul><p id="336b" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">2. In the <strong class="mm gu">Managed platform updates</strong>, leave all default values as selected by AWS.</p><p id="fe2c" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">3. Under <strong class="mm gu">Email notifications</strong>, to receive notifications about your environment, provide an email address and confirm your subscription to the Amazon SNS topic that Elastic Beanstalk creates for you.</p><p id="dc81" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">4. In the <strong class="mm gu">Rolling Updates and deployments</strong> section,</p><ul class=""><li id="4349" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under <strong class="mm gu">Application deployments</strong>,</li><li id="df79" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">On the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Deployment policy</em></strong> option, select <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Immutable</code>. This is the recommended approach for Docker applications. It creates new instances with the updated application version, ensuring a clean and reliable deployment process with minimal downtime.</li><li id="51f6" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">On the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Batch size type</em></strong>, select <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Fixed</code>. This ensures that if there is an update on the deployed instances, only one instance at a time will receive the updates.</li><li id="1088" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under the <strong class="mm gu">Configuration updates</strong> section, set the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Rolling update type</em></strong> to <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Immutable</code>.</li><li id="3f4b" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under <strong class="mm gu">Deployment preferences</strong>, customize the health check requirements and deployment timeouts as follows.</li><li id="c979" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">On the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Ignore health check</em></strong> option, select <code class="cw px py pz qa b">False</code> to maintain health checks to ensure instances meet your criteria before being considered healthy.</li><li id="2ea6" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">On the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Health threshold</em></strong>, select <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Ok</code> to use the default threshold, where all instances in a batch must pass health checks for the deployment to succeed.</li><li id="2f72" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">On the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Command timeout</em></strong>, increase the timeout to <code class="cw px py pz qa b">1000 seconds</code>.</li></ul><p id="2b7d" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">5. In the <strong class="mm gu">Platform software</strong>, configure the software that runs in the environment’s instances as follows:</p><ul class=""><li id="6e98" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">container options</em></strong>, from the <code class="cw px py pz qa b">proxy server</code> dropdown list, select <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Nginx</code>.</li><li id="dbc5" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Leave all other checkboxes in this sub-section unchecked to avoid unnecessary cost implications.</li><li id="2ea5" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Environment Properties</em></strong>, click on <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Add environment property</code> and set the <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Name</code> and <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Value</code> to <code class="cw px py pz qa b">PORT</code> and <code class="cw px py pz qa b">8501</code> respectively. The <em class="pw">Port 8501 is Exclusively set because Streamlit runs on port 8501</em></li></ul><p id="5053" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">6. Click <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Next</code> to Review the Environment&#x27;s Configuration</p><p id="8ad7" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">7. Click <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Submit</code> to initialize the provision and Deployment of the necessary resources.</p><blockquote class="qq qr qs"><p id="973c" class="mk ml pw mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">The deployment will take about 5 minutes and your instance health should transition to <code class="cw px py pz qa b">OK</code> as shown below.</p></blockquote></div></div></div><div class="ab ca oi oj ok ol" role="separator"><span class="om bx bl on oo op"></span><span class="om bx bl on oo op"></span><span class="om bx bl on oo"></span></div><div class="gm gn go gp gq"><div class="ab ca"><div class="ch bg fy fz ga gb"><h1 id="14f0" class="oq or gt be os ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn bj">Configuring the environment using the EB CLI</h1><p id="274b" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn po mp mq mr pp mt mu mv pq mx my mz pr nb nc nd ps nf ng nh gm bj">To create an <strong class="mm gu">Elastic Beanstalk environment</strong> using the <strong class="mm gu">EB CLI</strong>, follow these steps:</p><ol class=""><li id="984d" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh pt ob oc bj"><strong class="mm gu">Install the EB CLI</strong> (if you haven’t already):</li></ol><ul class=""><li id="4144" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">You can use the <a class="af pv" href="https://github.com/aws/aws-elastic-beanstalk-cli-setup" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">EB CLI setup scripts</a> available on GitHub to install the EB CLI on Linux, macOS, or Windows. These scripts handle dependencies and create a virtual environment for the EB CLI.</li><li id="0559" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Alternatively, you can <a class="af pv" href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/elasticbeanstalk/latest/dg/eb-cli3-install-advanced.html#eb-cli3-install-advanced.install" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">Manually install the EB CLI</a></li></ul><ol class=""><li id="4280" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh pt ob oc bj"><strong class="mm gu">Navigate to Your Project Directory</strong>:</li></ol><ul class=""><li id="0cb6" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Open your terminal or command prompt and navigate to the directory where your Elastic Beanstalk project resides.</li></ul><ol class=""><li id="98d8" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh pt ob oc bj"><strong class="mm gu">Create an Environment</strong>:</li></ol><ul class=""><li id="c77b" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Run the following command to first initialize an application that the environment will run on:</li></ul><pre class="nl nm nn no np qt qa qu bo qv ba bj"><span id="c328" class="qw or gt qa b bf qx qy l qz ra">eb init -i</span></pre><p id="caa1" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">The command will prompt you to</p><ul class=""><li id="de81" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Enter a default region: <em class="pw">Enter the number corresponding to your preferred region (default is 3)</em></li><li id="5810" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Select an application to use: <em class="pw">Enter the number corresponding to your desired application or create a new one</em></li><li id="03a8" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Confirm Docker usage: <em class="pw">Answer ‘y’ since the application is using Docker, otherwise ‘n’</em></li><li id="687b" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Select a platform branch: <em class="pw">Enter the number corresponding to </em><code class="cw px py pz qa b"><em class="pw">Docker running on 64bit Amazon Linux 2023</em></code><em class="pw"> platform</em></li><li id="b1fa" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Confirm CodeCommit setup: <em class="pw">Answer </em><code class="cw px py pz qa b"><em class="pw">n</em></code><em class="pw"> since we are not using CodeCommit, otherwise &#x27;Y&#x27;</em></li><li id="caf0" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Configure SSH for instances: <em class="pw">Answer </em><code class="cw px py pz qa b"><em class="pw">n</em></code><em class="pw"> since no set-up of SSH is necessary, otherwise &#x27;Y&#x27;</em></li><li id="5732" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Confirm Access Keys: <em class="pw">Input the access keys as prompted</em></li><li id="fbc0" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Run the following command to create an environment with the <code class="cw px py pz qa b">m5.large</code> instance type. Ensure to replace the env-name placeholder with your environment name.</li></ul><pre class="nl nm nn no np qt qa qu bo qv ba bj"><span id="e159" class="qw or gt qa b bf qx qy l qz ra">eb create &lt;env-name&gt; --vpc --instance-types m5a.large</span></pre><p id="d471" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">The EB CLI will prompt you for details such as <code class="cw px py pz qa b">VPC ID</code>, <code class="cw px py pz qa b">public IP address association</code>, <code class="cw px py pz qa b">list of Amazon EC2 subnets</code>, <code class="cw px py pz qa b">list of Amazon ELB subnets</code>, <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Public load balancer</code>, and <code class="cw px py pz qa b">list of Amazon VPC security groups</code>.</p><blockquote class="qq qr qs"><p id="56ef" class="mk ml pw mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">Ensure that in the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="gt">Load balancer subnets </em></strong>prompt, you select <em class="gt">one subnet from each Availability zone</em> and it is set to <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Public</code>, for it to serve requests from the internet.</p></blockquote><p id="93c4" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj"><strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">If your project directory contains source code, the EB CLI will bundle it up and deploy it to your environment.</em></strong></p></div></div></div><div class="ab ca oi oj ok ol" role="separator"><span class="om bx bl on oo op"></span><span class="om bx bl on oo op"></span><span class="om bx bl on oo"></span></div><div class="gm gn go gp gq"><div class="ab ca"><div class="ch bg fy fz ga gb"><p id="c29e" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj"><strong class="mm gu">Monitor Environment Status</strong>:</p><p id="6ff0" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">After creating the environment, you can check its status using:</p><pre class="nl nm nn no np qt qa qu bo qv ba bj"><span id="c118" class="qw or gt qa b bf qx qy l qz ra">eb status</span></pre><ul class=""><li id="634c" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">When the status is “Ready,” your application will be available at the domain URL provided on the environment dashboard, and the environment is ready for updates.</li></ul><p id="45ff" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj"><strong class="mm gu">View Health Information</strong>:</p><ul class=""><li id="36ce" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">To view health information about the instances in your environment, use:</li></ul><pre class="nl nm nn no np qt qa qu bo qv ba bj"><span id="ab4c" class="qw or gt qa b bf qx qy l qz ra">eb health</span></pre><ul class=""><li id="c2dd" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">You can also use the <code class="cw px py pz qa b">--refresh</code> option for an interactive view that updates every 10 seconds.</li></ul></div></div></div><div class="ab ca oi oj ok ol" role="separator"><span class="om bx bl on oo op"></span><span class="om bx bl on oo op"></span><span class="om bx bl on oo"></span></div><div class="gm gn go gp gq"><div class="ab ca"><div class="ch bg fy fz ga gb"><h1 id="d857" class="oq or gt be os ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn bj">Configuring the CICD pipeline from GitHub</h1><p id="83d5" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn po mp mq mr pp mt mu mv pq mx my mz pr nb nc nd ps nf ng nh gm bj">Before you begin</p><ul class=""><li id="b043" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Ensure your code is hosted in a <strong class="mm gu">GitHub repository</strong>.</li><li id="3a8b" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Ensure you have a running environment in Elastic Beanstalk</li><li id="98f9" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Make sure you have <strong class="mm gu">Administrator Access</strong> to the GitHub repository.</li></ul><p id="bb14" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">To configure <strong class="mm gu">AWS CodePipeline</strong> to deploy code from <strong class="mm gu">GitHub</strong> to <strong class="mm gu">AWS Elastic Beanstalk (EB)</strong> follow these steps:</p><ol class=""><li id="920e" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh pt ob oc bj">Open the <a class="af pv" href="https://console.aws.amazon.com/codesuite/codepipeline/pipelines" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank"><strong class="mm gu">AWS CodePipeline console</strong></a>, and click <strong class="mm gu">“Create pipeline”</strong>.</li><li id="ec3e" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh pt ob oc bj">In the <strong class="mm gu">Pipeline Settings</strong> section,</li></ol><ul class=""><li id="5830" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Pipeline name</em></strong>, choose a <em class="pw">pipeline name</em></li><li id="28ef" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">pipeline type</em></strong>, ensure that <code class="cw px py pz qa b">V2</code> is set.</li><li id="5522" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Execution mode</em></strong>, select <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Superseded</code></li><li id="cc7d" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Service role</em></strong> select <code class="cw px py pz qa b">New service role</code> and input a new or leave the auto-generated role name.</li><li id="9a8e" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Click <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Next</code> to go to step 3.</li></ul><p id="212f" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">3. In the <strong class="mm gu">Source</strong> Section,</p><ul class=""><li id="ca9a" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Source provider</em></strong>, select <code class="cw px py pz qa b">GitHub (Version 1)</code>.</li><li id="4861" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Connect your GitHub account and select the repository and branch you want to deploy.</li><li id="f2c0" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Under <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">Change detection options</em></strong>, ensure <code class="cw px py pz qa b">GitHub webhooks</code> is selected.</li><li id="01c0" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Click <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Next</code> to go to step 4.</li></ul><p id="bbed" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">4. In the <strong class="mm gu">Build stage</strong>, you can <code class="cw px py pz qa b">skip build stage</code>.</p><p id="5dc8" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">5. In the <strong class="mm gu">Deploy stage</strong>, choose <code class="cw px py pz qa b">Elastic Beanstalk</code> as the <strong class="mm gu"><em class="pw">deployment provider </em></strong>then select the application and environment you created earlier.</p><p id="0c96" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj"><strong class="mm gu">6. </strong>Review and Create the Pipeline</p><ul class=""><li id="2e1e" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Review your pipeline configuration.</li><li id="e44c" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Click <strong class="mm gu">“Create pipeline”</strong>. This may take a few minutes. Wait for all three stages to show the green check mark.</li></ul><blockquote class="rb"><p id="e619" class="rc rd gt be re rf rg rh ri rj rk nh dt">Any commits to the specified branch in your GitHub repository will now trigger the pipeline. CodePipeline will automatically deploy your code to Elastic Beanstalk based on the configuration you set up.</p></blockquote><ol class=""><li id="9739" class="mk ml gt mm b mn rl mp mq mr rm mt mu mv rn mx my mz ro nb nc nd rp nf ng nh pt ob oc bj"><strong class="mm gu">Monitor and Troubleshoot</strong>:</li></ol><ul class=""><li id="62ae" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Monitor your pipeline’s progress in the CodePipeline console.</li><li id="0fa8" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Check the Elastic Beanstalk environment logs for any deployment issues.</li></ul></div></div></div><div class="ab ca oi oj ok ol" role="separator"><span class="om bx bl on oo op"></span><span class="om bx bl on oo op"></span><span class="om bx bl on oo"></span></div><div class="gm gn go gp gq"><div class="ab ca"><div class="ch bg fy fz ga gb"><h1 id="7e13" class="oq or gt be os ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn bj">Troubleshooting</h1><p id="aaef" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn po mp mq mr pp mt mu mv pq mx my mz pr nb nc nd ps nf ng nh gm bj">This section provides some common issues and solutions for deploying the Streamlit application on Elastic Beanstalk, such as connection errors, timeout errors, or permission errors.</p><p id="9aa5" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">It also provides some tips and best practices for debugging and optimizing the Streamlit application.</p><figure class="nl nm nn no np nq ni nj paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="nr ns fi nt bg nu"><div class="ni nj rq"><picture><source bx bl on oo op"></span><span class="om bx bl on oo op"></span><span class="om bx bl on oo"></span></div><div class="gm gn go gp gq"><div class="ab ca"><div class="ch bg fy fz ga gb"><h1 id="ca82" class="oq or gt be os ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn bj"><strong class="al">Clean-up</strong></h1><p id="cbce" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn po mp mq mr pp mt mu mv pq mx my mz pr nb nc nd ps nf ng nh gm bj">If you do not want to incur more costs on the resources you have provisioned, you can choose to delete or terminate them.</p><p id="8edc" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">To start with,</p><ul class=""><li id="a13a" class="mk ml gt mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Detach any <strong class="mm gu">Elastic IP</strong> that could have been created.</li><li id="3e50" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Delete any <strong class="mm gu">NAT Gateways</strong> that could have been provisioned.</li><li id="d025" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Delete the <strong class="mm gu">Application Load Balancer</strong> that was created</li><li id="0338" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Terminate the <strong class="mm gu">ElasticBeanstalk</strong> environment you created as well as its respective application.</li><li id="a369" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Delete the <strong class="mm gu">S3 bucket</strong> provisioned by ElasticBeanstalk. You might need to update your bucket policy to Allow <code class="cw px py pz qa b">DeleteBucket</code></li><li id="3fec" class="mk ml gt mm b mn od mp mq mr oe mt mu mv of mx my mz og nb nc nd oh nf ng nh oa ob oc bj">Finally, delete the <strong class="mm gu">VPC</strong>. This will delete all the subnets, Internet gateways, route tables, security groups, and all other resources that accompany a VPC.</li></ul><blockquote class="qq qr qs"><p id="168b" class="mk ml pw mm b mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh gm bj">Thank you for reading my post please follow me on <a class="af pv" href="https://www.linkedin.com/in/francis-ndaruga/" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">Linkedin </a>as well as on <a class="af pv" href="https://twitter.com/ndaruga_" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">X(Formerly
